<page sig="a1r">
<section type="title-page">
<heading>
A NEW
DICTIONARY
OF THE
Terms Ancient and Modern
OF THE
Canting Crew.
In its several
TRIBES,
OF
<f type="i">Gypsies, Beggers, Thieves, Cheats</f>, &c.
WITH
An Addition of some Proverbs,
Phrases, Figurative Speeches, <f type="i">&c.</f>

Useful for all sorts of People, (especially
Foreigners) to secure their <f type="i">Money</f> and preserve their
<f type="i">Lives</f>; besides very Diverting and Entertaining, be&shy;
ing wholly New.
</heading>

By <f type="i">B. E.</f> Gent.

<f type="i">London</f>,
Printed for <f type="i">W. Hawes</f> at the <f type="i">Rose</f> in <f type="i">Ludgate-street,
P. Gilbourne</f> at the Corner of <f type="i">Chancery-lane</f> in <f type="i">Fleet-&shy;
street</f>, and <f type="i">W. Davis</f> at the <f type="i">Black Hill</f> in <f type="i">Cornhill</f>.
</section>
</page>

<page sig="a1v">
</page>

<page sig="a2r">
<section type="preface">
<heading>
THE
PREFACE.
</heading>

Before I present the Reader,
with the following Dictiona&shy;
ry of the <f type="i">Beggers</f> and <f type="i">Gypsies
Cant</f>, I think it not amiss to premise
a few Words concerning the <f type="i">Beg&shy;
gers</f> and <f type="i">Gypsies</f> themselves, by way
of an Historical Account, of the
Antiquity of the one, and the Uni&shy;
versality of the other.
It makes not a little for the Ho&shy;
nour of the <f type="i">Beggers</f>, that their Ori&shy;
ginal according to some Accounts,
is no less Ancient than that of <f type="i">Christi&shy;
</page>

<page sig="a2v">
<f type="i">anity</f> it self; for in the Opinion of
<f type="i">Charron</f>, as the <f type="i">Slaves</f> went off, the
<f type="i">Beggers</f> came in their Place. So
much at least is granted, That the
<f type="i">Jews</f> who allow'd of <f type="i">Slaves</f>, had no
<f type="i">Beggers</f>. What shall we say, but
that if it be true, that the Emanci&shy;
pating or Freeing of <f type="i">Slaves</f> as in&shy;
deed the making of <f type="i">Beggers</f>; it fol&shy;
lows that Christianity which is dai&shy;
ly employed in Redeeming <f type="i">Slaves</f>
from the <f type="i">Turks</f>, Ransom'd no less
than all at once from <f type="i">Pagan Slavery</f>
at first, at no dearer a Rate, than the
Rent-charge of maintaining the <f type="i">Beg&shy;
gers</f>, as the Price and Purchace of our
Freedoms
As for the Antiquity of the <f type="i">Eng&shy;
lish Beggers</f>, it may be observed, That
the first <f type="i">Statute</f> which makes Provi&shy;
sion for the <f type="i">Parish-Poor</f>, is no older
than Queen <f type="i">Elizabeth</f>; from which
it may be fairly Collected, That
</page>

<page sig="a3r">
they entred with us upon the <f type="i">Disso&shy;
lution</f> of the <f type="i">Abbeys</f>, as with them
abroad, upon the <f type="i">Delivery</f> of the
<f type="i">Slaves</f>.
For the <f type="i">Gypsies</f>, they and the <f type="i">Foul
Disease</f> have alike the Fate to run
through a <f type="i">Geography</f> of <f type="i">Names</f>, and
to be made free of as many <f type="i">Coun&shy;
tries</f>, as almost there are <f type="i">Languages</f> to
call them Names in for as the <f type="i">French</f>
call the <f type="i">Pox</f>, the <f type="i">Italian</f> Disease, they
again give it to the <f type="i">Spaniards</f>, as these
to the <f type="i">French</f>; so the <f type="i">French</f> call the
Gypsies <f type="i">Boemie</f>, or <f type="i">Bohemians</f>, belike,
because they made their first Appea&shy;
rance in <f type="i">Bohemia</f> of any Part of
<f type="i">Europe</f>; the <f type="i">Italians</f> Name them
<f type="i">Zingari</f> or <f type="i">Saracens</f>, the <f type="i">Spaniards
Itanos</f> as we <f type="i">Egyptians</f>; whether it
be, that the <f type="i">Italians</f> give them the
<f type="i">Turks</f>, as the <f type="i">Spaniards</f> give them
the <f type="i">Moors</f>, as being both the next
Neighbors to each; I take not up&shy;
</page>

<page sig="a3v">
on me to Determine, only it may
be observed, betwixt the Comple&shy;
ment of either kind, the Odds is no
greater than this, of giving a Nati&shy;
on a Clap, or of laying a brood of
Bastards at it's Door.
Through <f type="i">Holland</f> has no Beggers,
if the <f type="i">Dutch</f> themselves are not the
greatest Beggers in the World; and
<f type="i">Switzerland</f> has no Thieves, if the
<f type="i">Swiss</f> who are altogether Soldiers, are
not the greatest of Thieves. Yet, I
say, neither the <f type="i">States</f> that are with&shy;
out <f type="i">Beggers</f>, nor the <f type="i">Cantons</f> that
are without <f type="i">Thieves</f>, are notwith&shy;
standing either the one or the other,
without <f type="i">Gypsies</f>. So as what they
want of <f type="i">Beggers</f> and <f type="i">Thieves</f> in point
of Antiquity, the <f type="i">Gypsies</f> claim a&shy;
bove both, in point of Universality.
But though <f type="i">Gypsies</f> are found in
all Christian Countries, yet are they
not in all Countries alike; their Na&shy;
</page>

<page sig="a4r">
ture and Genius being diverse, in pro&shy;
portion to the Countries amongst
whom they Stroul; so that the same
Question remains upon them, as is
started of the <f type="i">Winds</f>, as Universal
Travellers as the <f type="i">Gypsies</f>, that it seems
a Doubt, Whether they partake more
of the Nature of the Countries
whence they rise, or of those through
which they Pass?
Nor is it also new to meet the
<f type="i">Beggers</f> and the <f type="i">Proverbs</f> together,
for the Fashion is as old as <f type="i">Plautus</f>,
who put the Proverbs and the Jests
in the Mouth of his <f type="i">Slaves</f>. And in
the Character of <f type="i">Sancho Pancha, Cer&shy;
vantes</f> has Trod in the same Steps;
in the History of <f type="i">Don Quixot, San&shy;
cho</f> being distinguished no less by his
<f type="i">Proverbs</f>, than his <f type="i">Asse</f>. And be&shy;
tween the <f type="i">Slaves</f> and the <f type="i">Beggers</f>,
the Difference is no greater, than be&shy;
tween <f type="i">Fathers</f> and their <f type="i">Heirs</f>.
</page>

<page sig="a4v">
if some Terms and Phrases of
better Quality and Fashion, keep so
ill Company, as Tag-Rag and Long&shy;
Tail; you are to remember, that it
is no less than Customary, for <f type="i">Great
Persons</f> a broad to hide themselves
often in Disguise among the <f type="i">Gypsies</f>;
and even the late L. of <f type="i">Rochester</f> a&shy;
mong us, when time was, among o&shy;
ther Frolicks, was not ashamed to
keep the <f type="i">Gypsies</f> Company.
</section>
</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lexeme="bacon(n)">Bacon,</form> <xpln>as <f type="i">he sav'd his
